Current Situation of Education in the Special District of Eastern Provinces 96

Paying Attention to the Education of Naturalized White Russian Children

The education sector in the Special District of Eastern Provinces has made considerable progress in recent years. There are currently eight male middle schools, two female middle schools, one industrial high school, more than seventy primary schools, and three specialized schools (medical, fine arts, and normal), but not including universities. All schools below the specialized level are directly under the jurisdiction of the Education Department. There are also more than thirty schools for children of Soviet railway employees and more than sixty Russian侨schools, which are also under the jurisdiction of the Education Department. The current Director is Mr. Zhang Guochen, who has only been in office for one year and has worked hard to govern, making much progress in educational facilities. Within the Department, he has organized various committees to discuss matters of reform. Important ones include the Committee for Revising Regulations, the Committee for Reviewing the Education of Naturalized Children, the Committee for Clearing the Education Funds in Arrears for the Seventeenth Year, the Committee for Reorganizing Russian僑Schools, the Committee for Literary and Artistic Review, and the Committee for Planning School Buildings, not to mention the Administrative Conference, the Education Conference, and the Joint Conference of Principals. Among the various committees, the Committee for Reviewing the Education of Naturalized Children is the most valuable. Most of the White Russians in the Special District have been naturalized as Chinese citizens, but in the past, no attention has been paid to the education of their children. Often, the father is a Chinese citizen, but the children still attend Russian侨schools, and although they are nominally Chinese, they do not know Chinese, and remain alienated from the Chinese. This is very different from the original intention of allowing them to naturalize. Mr. Zhang organized the committee to discuss reforming this malpractice. However, due to various difficulties, the result of the discussion was to start with the young, that is, the naturalized children who have just reached school age. From this year, they will all be required to enter Chinese schools and will not be allowed to be admitted or transferred to Russian僑schools or other schools. Those who have already entered other schools and are younger and in lower grades will also be transferred to Chinese schools, with the aim of gradually making naturalized children (i.e., those who have become citizens) receive complete Chinese education. This measure not only concerns the education of naturalized children, but also brings unlimited benefits to the Northeast, especially along the Eastern Railway, in the future. In terms of schools, those newly established last year include the Fine Arts Specialized School, the Eighth Male Middle School, the Second Female Middle School, and the Twenty-Fourth Primary School in the First School District, as well as the recovery of the Normal School run by Russian僑schools, the establishment of a Russian Language Normal College, and the addition of more than twenty grades to various primary schools. This year, two more primary schools will be added in Shuangchengpu and Erdahezi, and it is planned to add ten more primary school grades, all with funding, and work has begun.

[L Ministry of Agriculture and Mining Focuses on Mining Education>

Circular Orders All Provinces to Investigate Mining Schools

In order to focus on mining education, the Ministry of Agriculture and Mining specifically ordered the Mining Administration Department of the Ministry to formulate a general table of mining education in the country, and yesterday issued a circular to the Agricultural and Mining Construction Departments of all provinces to conduct a detailed investigation of the situation and nature of mining specialized schools in their respective provinces, fill in the information, and report it for consolidation.

Jiangsu Education Department Issues Circular Stipulating That Education Fees Must Not Be Changed 97

The Jiangsu Provincial Education Department issued instructions to the directors of the education bureaus of sixty-one counties, saying: It is hereby notified that increasing education funding and guaranteeing its independence are included in the political program. Most of the education funding in various counties of the province is dedicated funds. Whether the name has been clearly designated as education fees, or the name is not education fees, but it has long been designated as education fees and has been included in the budget for many years, it must not be arbitrarily changed. The previous Central Executive Yuan has repeatedly ordered various counties to comply with this. However, recently, it has been found that Dongtai, Taixing, and other counties have proposed to divert the funds for local chronicles and rural administration, which have long been designated as education fees, to other uses. It should be that violating the established plan hinders education fees. After consultation with the Finance Department and the dispatch of personnel for investigation, it has been strictly ordered not to allow it. At the beginning of political tutelage, it is extremely important to vigorously promote the popularization of education. Education funding is being increased year by year in order to gradually expand the undertaking and achieve the goal of popularization. If the inherent funding that has been decided can be arbitrarily overturned, not only will the existing undertaking be affected, but education funding will also lose its guarantee, which is contrary to the party's emphasis on education. It is hereby reiterated that all education funding that has been decided in various counties, whether the name has been corrected or not, and has been allocated as education fees in fact, must not be changed without authorization. In addition to submitting a request to the provincial government to issue a circular to all counties to comply with this, and issuing separate orders, it is hereby ordered to be notified. This order.

Jiangsu Education Department Stipulates the Effective Period of Certified Teachers 98

The Jiangsu Education Department previously organized a Committee for Certifying Primary School Teachers and formulated regulations in order to focus on teachers' qualifications, preparing to implement certification. However, the regulations did not clearly stipulate the effective period of certified primary school teachers at the time in order to meet the needs, which was inconvenient in implementation. The Department has now formulated six provisional standards for the effective period of certified primary school teachers in Jiangsu Province and announced them for implementation. In the future, matters concerning requests to extend the effective period will be handled in accordance with these standards. The standards are recorded as follows:

Provisional Standards for the Effective Period of Certified Primary School Teachers in Jiangsu Province

(1) The effective period of all primary school teachers who have passed the Jiangsu Provincial Examination and Certification is provisionally set at five years. (2) Primary school teachers who have passed the certification and meet the following requirements within the effective period may extend their effective period separately, but not exceeding three years at most. (3) Those who meet one of the following items may extend the effective period by one year: A. Those who have selected and studied two or more education courses in the summer school or summer vacation training course established by a national university or a registered private university and specialized school and have obtained a certificate of qualification; B. Those who have selected and studied education courses in the local education district research association or provincial middle school normal department and the summer vacation training course established by the education bureau of each county with the approval of the Education Department and have obtained a certificate of qualification with eight or more credits; C. Those who have served as primary school teachers for more than five years and have received excellent comments from provincial and county supervisors and education committee members during the effective period. (4) Those who meet one of the following items may extend the effective period by two years: A. Those who have studied in the summer school or summer vacation training course established by a national university or a registered private university and specialized school for more than two times, each selecting two or more education courses and obtaining a certificate of qualification; B. Those who have studied in the local education district research association, provincial middle school normal department, and the summer vacation training course established by the education bureau of each county with the approval of the Education Department for two times, each selecting education courses and obtaining a certificate of qualification with eight or more credits; C. Those who have served as primary school teachers for more than five years and have received excellent comments from provincial and county supervisors and education committee members for more than two times during the effective period. (5) Those who meet one of the following items may extend the effective period by three years: A. Those who have studied in a national university or a registered private university and specialized school for more than one year during the effective period and have obtained a certificate of achievement; B. Those who have served as primary school teachers for more than five years, have a thorough understanding of education principles and teaching methods, and have specialized writings or special achievements that have been commended by the Education Department. (6) These standards have been announced and implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Education Department and submitted to the Provincial Government and the Ministry of Education for record.

Seal for Municipal and County Education Branch Associations 99

Issued by the Education Bureau

The Jiangsu Education Department previously submitted to the Ministry of Education, based on the report from the Wuxi Education Bureau, asking which agency should issue the seal for the municipal and county education branch associations. Recently, it received instructions from the Ministry of Education, saying: The report is known. It is found that the municipal and county education branch associations may use seals similar to those used by the county education associations, and the municipal and county education associations shall submit a request to the competent municipal and county education bureau for issuance. The material and size shall comply with the Regulations on Seals issued by the National Government and the attached seal diagram (the seal is made of wood, square, with each side measuring five and two-tenths centimeters, and shall be handled. It is hereby ordered to comply with this and forward it for notification. This order.

This City

Director Chen of the Municipal Education Bureau Requests 103

Abolishing the University Preparatory System

The Shanghai Special Municipal Education Bureau submitted a document to the Ministry of Education yesterday, saying: A document is submitted to request the abolition of the university preparatory system for inspection and verification. It is believed that the establishment of a university is originally intended to study advanced academics and cultivate specialized talents. Its students must have a foundation in learning and be of appropriate age to be able to receive university education. Recently, it has been found that many universities in the country have preparatory departments attached to them, recruiting students who do not have the qualifications to enter the university, or even setting a preparatory period of three years and recruiting students who have just graduated from junior high school, nominally preparing for entering the regular department, giving young people the opportunity to study, but in fact disrupting the academic system and reducing the level of students. The original term of study for high school is three years, and the university preparatory is also set at three years, which is already inappropriate, such as only two years or one year, then the distinction is even more inappropriate. This is the first aspect that is not suitable in terms of academic programs. University training and management are relatively relaxed in all aspects in fact. Students must be of a certain age to avoid abuses. A junior high school graduate is only about fifteen years old. The age difference is too large. Studying in a school is not suitable for management. This is the second aspect that is not suitable. Moreover, according to the University Organization Law and the University Regulations, there is no provision for a preparatory department. However, domestic universities still set up preparatory departments, and private universities take this opportunity to widely recruit. All young people with shallow academic abilities flock to them for vain reputation, supply and demand correspond to each other and are used by each other, and the level of universities is declining day by day, and middle schools cannot be managed. The relationship with national education is very great. The bureau of directors sees the inappropriateness of the preparatory department, and in order to seek rectification, it specifically submitted the 136th bureau affairs meeting for resolution, requesting your department to issue a clear order to abolish the university preparatory system within a time limit. If it is necessary to establish a preparatory department, such as medical and engineering colleges that need to make up for German, and the connection method for students who have graduated from the old system of middle schools, please also order to comply with it. It will be beneficial to the students' study and self-cultivation. Is there anything appropriate? It is submitted for inspection and instructed to comply with it, which is in the public interest. Respectfully presented to Minister Jiang of the Ministry of Education, Chen Dezheng, Director of the Shanghai Special Municipal Education Bureau.

A Record of the Opening Ceremony of Jianguo Middle School 105

Principal Chen Gave Earnest Instructions

Jianguo Middle School on Zhiyuan Road in Zhabei, this city, has long been open. The first memorial week of this semester was held a few days ago, and the opening ceremony was held to make up for it. About 150 teachers, staff, and students attended. The ceremony was presided over by Mr. Chen Dezheng, the principal of the school. After the ceremony, Principal Chen gave a report on current affairs. After the report, he gave an earnest speech, mainly divided into the following three points: First, students must strictly abide by school rules, not only must they rectify order, but they should also work hard to study. Studying is not for fame and profit, but a necessary condition for survival. Therefore, all fluke thoughts should be eliminated. Second, students should study diligently and abide by the rules. Teachers and staff should set an example and be a model for students. The teachers and staff of this school are purely knowledgeable people, and students will benefit a lot from their teaching. However, there may be those who neglect to teach due to negligence. It has been instructed that the academic affairs department should pay close attention to this. If a teacher is absent from teaching once, the school will give a warning. If a teacher is absent from teaching twice, in addition to a serious warning, an appropriate punishment will be given. If a teacher is absent from teaching more than three times, another teacher will be hired immediately. The reason why the school advocates such strictness is entirely to respect students' studies. Therefore, students should follow school rules, respect teachers, and work hard at their studies. Third, co-education of men and women has become a major problem in education, but we still need to test it. During this test period, male and female students in our school must respect each other. Except for classes and self-study, male and female students must not joke with each other, nor may they enter each other's boarding places. Those who violate this will be immediately expelled and must leave the school within five minutes. This issue is not only related to students' studies, but also to the future of co-education of men and women. After the speech, the meeting adjourned.

Recent News from the Music Research Association 109

The Shanghai Music Research Association in Hengqing Lane, Bailey Road, is the only association in Shanghai for amateur Western music learners. It has been established for 11 years. The association aims to cultivate musical talents. Therefore, it usually focuses on the training of scholars and does not participate in any group gatherings. This session is the 22nd session to recruit male and female students. The subjects are divided into piano, violin, singing, theory, etc. The professors are all music experts in Shanghai. In addition to the above courses, the association has added a singing class this session, specializing in teaching various famous songs from Shanghai sound films, taught by singer Zhong Zitong. Classes are coming soon. Those who are interested in music can go to register immediately. For regulations, send a letter with a one-point postage.

(1) The Construction of the Venue Will Be Completed Soon

All Ball Fields Can Be Completed Immediately

Part of the Racetrack Has Been Completed

The Command Platform Is Being Built in Full Swing

The Construction of the Two Main Gates Is Quite Magnificent

Since the preparatory office of the National Games moved to Meidong Gaoqiao, the work has been proceeding very intensely. The construction of the venue has been supervised by Zhu Yaoting, the staff member of the engineering section, who urged the contractors to speed up the construction. So far, the scale has gradually been completed. All the football fields, tennis courts, baseball fields, and basketball courts in the venue will be completed soon. As for the racetrack, a part of the near west has been completed, and only a small section is still implementing heavy pressure machine work, which can be completely completed immediately. As for the stands, the command platform, and the military band platform, they are being built in full swing these days, and they can be completed within the deadline. The surrounding walls of the venue have been ordered to be whitewashed separately, and they have been renewed, and they are no longer the old view. The main gate of the conference is divided into two seats on the left and right, which is quite magnificent. The roads along the way are also built by the Public Works Bureau, and they will be completely completed in early March.

Recording the Content of the Conference

Guiding the South Needle for Visitors

Jiangsu Provincial Games 111

The Jiangsu Provincial Games are divided into two types, A and B. Type A is the 3rd Provincial Secondary School Games, which will be held from the 15th to the 17th. Type B is the Jiangsu Provincial Mass Preliminary for the National Games, which will be held from the 18th to the 20th. The sports competition rules, etc., were known to this newspaper on February 1. Now, the mass preliminary competition regulations are recorded below.

Regulations for Public Preliminary Competitions 112

A. Track and Field (1) Athletes will participate as individuals; (2) Each athlete may participate in one to four events; (3) Each athlete may not participate in both the decathlon and pentathlon simultaneously; (4) Participants must register with the association by the specified date (registration forms will be provided separately); (5) The top three athletes in each event will be selected; (6) Athletes must abide by the competition rules and maintain order throughout the venue; (7) Athletes participating in the competition must pay a registration fee (the amount will be determined separately).

B. Ball Games (1) Teams will participate as units. The regulations for the number of players per team are as follows: 1. Soccer: 13 players; 2. Basketball: Men, 10 players; Women, 12 players; 3. Volleyball: Men, 12 players; Women, 15 players; 4. Tennis: Doubles and singles (limited to 6 players); (2) The competition will use an elimination system. The order will be determined by the committee through a drawing of lots; (3) Each team should arrive at the venue on time. Teams arriving more than ten minutes late will be considered to have forfeited; (4) Teams wishing to participate in the competition must register with the association by the specified date (registration forms will be provided separately); (5) If there are protests regarding the referees, they must be submitted in writing to the committee on the same day after the competition ends and await processing. Teams must not withdraw from the competition midway without cause. Violators will be considered to have forfeited; (6) Competition balls will be provided by the association.

C. Accommodation for Athletes Coming to the Province to Participate in the Games: 1. Accommodation will be arranged near the association on behalf of the athletes. Athletes must bring their own luggage, washbasins, etc.; 2. Athletes are responsible for their own meals and travel expenses.

D. Registration Deadline: Registration will close at 6:00 PM on March 10th. (All participants must send their registration forms to the association before 6:00 PM on March 10th; they should not be mailed from various places on the 10th). Late registrations will not be accepted. E. Number of Athletes Selected: The top three athletes in each track and field event will be selected. (Note: Whether athletes will be sent to the National Games will still be subject to review by the association's selection committee).

F. Meeting Date and Location: The meeting venue is at the large parade ground outside the Zhenjiang South Gate, from 8:00 AM on March 18th to 6:00 PM on March 20th.

G. All rules will be implemented in accordance with the latest Far Eastern Games rules. H. Check-in: Athletes must check in with the association before 6:00 PM on the 17th to receive their numbers, pins, etc.

Local News

Customs Gold Market Conversion Standard 118

To Be Announced Daily Starting Next Month

Using HSBC Exchange Rate as Standard

After the Jianghai Customs changed to a gold unit system for collecting taxes, the daily exchange rate for various currencies was originally converted and announced by the Customs in advance. Now, due to frequent changes in exchange rates and excessive fluctuations in gold prices, it has been revised to be converted and announced daily. The Ministry of Finance has issued instructions to follow suit. The Inspector General of Customs has officially issued an announcement, which will be officially implemented from the day after tomorrow (March 1st). From then on, the conversion rate will be announced daily at 9:30 AM at the Jianghai Customs and the Central Bank Tax Collection Office. This conversion rate is based on the HSBC exchange rate.

Government States Its Position on Raw Silver Imports 119

No Import Tax Levied

No Restrictive Measures Implemented

Minister Song announced yesterday that the government has decided not to levy import duties on raw silver and will not implement other measures to restrict the import of raw silver. The world silver market has been showing signs of fluctuation due to the government's undecided attitude. After the announcement of this decision, it should be able to clarify the government's attitude.

Two Groups Pay Attention to the Sino-Japanese Reciprocal Treaty 120

Flour Association Telegram to Nanjing Executive Yuan President, Foreign Minister, Finance Minister, and Industry and Commerce Minister: Our country's industry and commerce are bound by tariff treaties and have no room for development. However, reports state that the Sino-Japanese Tariff Treaty Reciprocal Agreement will exchange raw materials for manufactured products. In terms of the flour industry, Japanese flour will be imported as much as possible, and the sales in the three northeastern provinces will be completely occupied. Japanese wheat has no seeds for Chinese factories to use. Reciprocity is an empty word, and Chinese factories will suffer real harm. We urge you to insist that Japanese flour be excluded from the reciprocal treaty and request that the full text of the treaty be disclosed before signing to show great faith and comply with public opinion. We await your orders with anticipation. Shanghai Machine Flour Company Association Chairman Gu Lugui, Sun Jingxi, Rong Zongjin, respectfully.

Machine Federation Telegram to Nanjing National Government, sent to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, Foreign Affairs, and Finance: Reports state that a new Sino-Japanese treaty is being drafted, and more than 100 types of goods with reciprocal tariff rates have been determined between China and Japan, including cotton yarn and cotton cloth. The Japanese imports are all industrial re-manufactured products, and the Chinese exports are all raw materials. The current situation of the Chinese cotton textile industry is in a critical period. The establishment of this reciprocal treaty will condemn the cotton textile industry to death. It is greatly related to the national economy and the people's livelihood. Please pay attention to maintain the lifeblood of domestic goods and prevent other countries from following suit. Shanghai Machine-Made National Goods Factory Federation, You.

Japanese Ship Causes Another Disaster 121

Damaging Chinese Ship. The cargo ship Kakomaru of the Japanese Mail Steamship Company, Shanghai-New York route, with a deadweight of over 6,500 tons, departed from Hong Kong to Shanghai on the 23rd of this month. On the way, due to heavy fog at sea, the ship continued to sound its whistle while sailing and did not stop. On the 24th, the fog at sea had not completely cleared. The Kakomaru ship, in this heavy fog, arrived at the port of Fuzhou, where a Chinese ship named Dongyu was coming. The Japanese ship collided with the hull of the Dongyu ship. Because the Japanese ship was huge and the Dongyu ship was small, the Japanese ship was only slightly damaged after the collision, while the damage to the Chinese ship was very severe. The Japanese ship Kakomaru has now returned to Hong Kong. The Japanese Mail Steamship Company has received a telegram from the ship stating that it needs to be slightly repaired in Hong Kong. As for the details of the damage to the Dongyu, there has been no report by telegram, so it is not clear. A telegram was sent here yesterday to inquire.

Overturning a Civilian Boat The Japanese Mail Steamship Company's Moji-Yokohama route ship Mikasasanmaru, having loaded cargo in Shanghai, set off for Japan. When leaving the port, the company sent a small tugboat, the Jinlingmaru, to tow it out of the port. At that time, there were four cargo barges crossing the bow of the Mikasasanmaru. One of the cargo barges collided with the starboard side of the Mikasasanmaru, and the civilian boat immediately overturned, the cargo was lost, and the boatmen fell into the water. The Japanese ship rescued the people in the water. The Japanese maritime officer stationed in Shanghai agreed to repair the damaged civilian boat and immediately ordered the Mikasasanmaru to continue its voyage to Japan as usual.

Municipal Port Authority Rectifies the Pudong Coastline 122

The Shanghai Municipal Port Authority has submitted a report to the Municipal Government to rectify the Pudong coastline: "The submission is to report the investigation of the Pudong coastline in this city and to propose rectification methods, requesting review and approval. It is found that only the area of the southern part of the city south of the Huangpu River has previously stipulated rectification methods. The rest of the area north of Puxi is within the concession area and is not easy to start with for a while. The Wusong River coastline is narrow and not suitable for rent, which hinders traffic. However, the Pudong coastline has a very wide area and is under the jurisdiction of this city. Investigation and rectification are urgent. This bureau once sent staff member Wu Zhiyi and surveyor Yuan Baoyan to investigate and measure. After the survey was completed, the survey situation was reported in writing, and a list of Pudong coastline users and a percentage table of the coastline occupied by Chinese and foreign merchants were attached. After reviewing the staff member's report, the Pudong coastline stretches from Zhoujiadu to Qingning Temple, with a total length of 15,460 meters. There are more than 70 merchants, including 31 merchants from British, French, American, and Japanese groups, occupying 66% of the entire coastline. The land used by each merchant is dozens of acres or more, each with its own walls and guards, and there are no roads for passage. The businesses operated by each merchant are mostly wharves, warehouses, docks, shipyards, oil factories, and storage areas. According to Article 12 of the Sino-British Supplementary Treaty of the eighth year of Xianfeng in the former Qing Dynasty, British people were allowed to rent land to build houses and warehouses in the trading ports. In addition, Article 6 of the Sino-British Supplementary Treaty of Commerce and Navigation in the 28th year of Guangxu in the former Qing Dynasty stated that China agreed to set up more customs warehouses in the trading ports to store foreign goods. The treaty chapters of the United States and France also stipulate that merchants of those countries can set up warehouses in the trading ports. From the above treaty chapters, it seems that foreign merchants have the possibility of building warehouses in the trading ports. However, the Shanghai British and French Concession Land Regulations state that land rental within the boundary clearly mentions the words 'within the boundary', which means restricting areas outside the boundary. Therefore, foreign merchants should limit themselves to the concession area when building warehouses in trading ports. As for the navigation treaty, the phrase 'China agrees to set up more customs warehouses' indicates that foreign merchants are not allowed to operate their own warehouses, so they requested the establishment of more warehouses in the treaty, which is very clear. The treaty chapter does not specify the wharves. However, the regulations for ships sailing in the inner harbor only allow foreign merchants to rent warehouses, and wharves cannot be built by foreign merchants themselves. Now the Pudong area is not a concession. According to the treaty chapters, foreign merchants are not allowed to build wharves and warehouses. However, illegal construction has become a fact. The only way to remedy this is to manage it and make it comply with the laws and regulations of this city, and then formulate a plan for recovery. The bureau intends to issue the current regulations for citizens renting the coastline separately. All those who have set up wharves and warehouses along the Pudong coast and use the coastline must comply with the regulations. The bureau will sign contracts and collect coastline rental and deposit fees to rectify the situation. In the future, citizens who request to set up warehouses, wharves, and rent the coastline must apply to the bureau for approval. In this way, the past can be rectified and the future can be restricted, and the coastline fee can also increase the city's revenue by about 100,000 yuan per year. All the reasons for the investigation of the Pudong coastline and the proposed rectification methods, along with a copy of the report, a list of Pudong coastline users, a percentage table of the coastline occupied by Chinese and foreign merchants, and a transcript of the full text of each treaty chapter, are hereby submitted to the mayor for review to determine whether they are appropriate. Waiting for instructions. It is heard that after receiving the report, Mayor Zhang instructed the bureau: 'The report is fully understood. The proposed rectification methods for the Pudong coastline can recover sovereignty and increase revenue, so they should be approved. The relevant bureaus should be asked to cooperate and carry out the work diligently. However, the situation of the coastline, as stated in the last item of the report and the last item of the coastline list, regarding Hefeng and Hexing, are clearly different. Please clarify whether this is a typographical error and report back.' This order."

Japanese Expel Chinese Again 123

A Total of Three Groups

After a group of overseas Chinese went to Japan on the 5th of this month to seek a living and were expelled back to Shanghai by the Japanese, Chinese people who went to Japan from then on regarded it as a dangerous path. Unexpectedly, in the past few days, there have been three consecutive incidents of the Japanese authorities expelling Chinese people. One group was Chen Shoutong, Lu Haoran, Wu Zuosheng, Zhou Yuanlong, and others who went to the islands under Yokohama Prefecture and Asakusa, etc. One group was Wu Peichuan who went to Nagoya, and one group was Lin Zhongxin, Weng Yizhen, Chen Shimei, and others who went to Moji and Asakusa. Among them, some were prevented from landing because they claimed to be ill, and others were rejected from landing because they did not comply with the entry regulations. All of them have been escorted onto Japanese ships and sent back to Shanghai. Among them, there are people from Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong, and most of them are in the catering and barber industries.

Shanghai Charitable Organizations Federation Calls for Peace 124

The Shanghai Charitable Organizations Federation sent a telegram to Commander-in-Chief Jiang and Vice Commander-in-Chief Yan: "Nanjing Commander-in-Chief Jiang, Taiyuan Vice Commander-in-Chief Yan, reports state that you two have exchanged telegrams, urging each other with righteousness. Although your political views are different, your love for the country is the same. However, rumors arise from nowhere, and gossip spreads, claiming that war is imminent, causing panic and stagnation in commerce, presenting a turbulent situation. Our country has been plagued by disasters for years, and the people's suffering has reached its extreme. Fortunately, you two have worked together to maintain the overall situation. If misunderstandings and rumors become reality, it would not be your original intention. The provinces affected by disasters in recent years are in urgent need of relief, and they are currently requesting funds to rush to carry out spring relief. Planting and cultivation are the only hope for farmers this year. If war breaks out, it will affect all provinces, and if cultivation is missed, the autumn harvest will be hopeless, which will inevitably lead to the whole country becoming disaster areas and all people becoming disaster victims. Even with relief funds, how can we start? Moreover, at a time when the financial situation is chaotic and the whole country is on the verge of bankruptcy? We earnestly request you two to pay attention to the people's livelihood, follow the people's will, work together, and quell the war, so that the dying life of the people across the country will not be extinguished along with the great calamity. We take the liberty to make these statements, filled with trepidation. Please consider it. Shanghai Charitable Organizations Federation Chairman Wang Zhen, Vice Chairman Huang Qinglan, respectfully."

Dai Jitao and Others Return to Shanghai Today 126

To Go to Nanjing Tonight to Report to Chiang

Dai Jitao, President of the Examination Yuan, and Zhu Jiahua, Director of the Civil Affairs Department of Zhejiang Province, went to Guangdong on official business and had successive discussions with the Guangdong authorities, resulting in considerable progress. On the 25th, they took the President Cleveland of the Dollar Steamship Line from Hong Kong back to Shanghai. They are expected to land at the New Customs Wharf at 2 p.m. today. Dai and others plan to go to Nanjing tonight to report the process to Chairman Chiang.

German Counselor Fischer to Go to Nanjing Tonight 127

German Counselor Fischer is scheduled to take the night train to Nanjing tonight to meet with Minister Wang and discuss important official matters. He requested the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to prepare a car yesterday, it is said.

Minquan Warship to Join the Fleet Soon 128

The newly built Minquan warship of the Ministry of the Navy, after its test run and gunnery trials at Wusongkou some time ago, has been arranging various internal equipment, such as wireless radio and searchlights, for days. This work is now complete. The ship's wireless radio is divided into two rooms, one for shortwave, dedicated to communication with the coast and various ships, and one for longwave, directly reaching foreign countries. The captain of the ship is Zheng Yaoshu, and the deputy captain is Nie Zhixiong. Before Zheng returns from Germany, Luo Zhitong, captain of the Weisheng warship, will temporarily act as captain. It is heard that the ship will receive an order from the central government within a week at the latest and will be incorporated into the Second Fleet to defend the Yangtze River.

Case of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau 129

Opinions For and Against Both Sides

Minister Wang's Talk

Minister Wang of the Ministry of Communications, regarding the

Page 14

establishment of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, spoke with reporters from various newspapers, saying: The reporter asked, when will the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau be established? What is the original intention of its establishment and what business will it operate in the future? Can the Minister tell us? The answer is: The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau is scheduled to open in Shanghai on March 15. After the establishment of the bureau, the post office will continue to handle matters related to reserve funds and remittances as before. However, the bureau will be specifically responsible for the design, management, supervision, etc., of special savings and remittances. In essence, it is just to introduce banking science into postal savings and remittance affairs. The reason why the government has specifically established a bureau to manage this matter is because the history of postal service in our country, although it has been more than 30 years, and there are already thousands of post offices in the interior, and the annual amount of remittances has exceeded tens of millions, the annual expenditure on remittance discounts alone is as high as more than three million yuan. Although these discounts can be slightly offset by remittance fee income, the postal remittance locations are so extensive that, even if we only consider the domestic remittance part, if we use banking specialization and science for management, the aforementioned expenditure of more than three million yuan, even if it cannot be completely eliminated, can still be reduced to some extent. If managed properly, it can even generate a surplus. The foreign exchange part is even more complicated due to the difference in gold and silver standards. At a time when gold is expensive and silver is cheap, it cannot be handled well without the participation of banking experts. As for the savings part, in terms of the amount received in the past ten years, there has indeed been some progress. However, if the personnel who have been handling postal savings and remittances are supplemented with the planning of banking experts, its development can be even more limitless. Modern economic undertakings have reached the degree of specialized division of labor and scientification. Postal specialization is not something that only those with banking knowledge can understand, and banking specialization is also difficult for postal personnel to master. The reason why postal services in various countries must specifically establish bureaus for the savings and remittance industries and employ specialized personnel to assist in management is not without reason. In the past 20 years, our country's postal affairs have increased tenfold, and economic surplus and deficit are so subtle, and their changes are extremely drastic. Therefore, the system of post offices concurrently handling savings and remittances is also not allowed by the times. Although a special bureau is established this time, the implementation of savings and remittance affairs still requires the transfer of experienced personnel from post offices to participate in the management, which is also to integrate postal experience and banking experience, so that the postal service can have hope for full development. According to its principle, it is nothing more than adopting the spirit of division of labor economy and scientific economy to adapt to the needs of the times. It is not just copying the established methods of various countries, regardless of the domestic situation. The reporter asked, the Shanghai Postal Workers' Union still has doubts about the Savings and Remittance Bureau. Has the Minister read it? The answer is: The Postal Workers' Union's presentation was read in the newspaper before it was submitted to the Ministry. Its content is roughly divided into five points: (A) The post office's savings and remittance business has not yet developed, and there is no need to establish a special bureau. (B) Savings and remittance affairs will be separated from the post office, and management and governance will not be specialized, which will inevitably lead to both sides losing. (C) The Savings and Remittance Bureau has no gold reserves or fund allocation. (D) If remittance and transfer affairs imitate banking methods, it will inevitably cause difficulties for inland post offices. (E) The selection and employment of personnel are not in accordance with the regulations of the postal service. I have carefully read it and am very disappointed. From the first point, savings and remittance affairs cannot be managed without banking specialization, as mentioned above. Handling savings is not just about receiving and paying savings. How to adjust the interest rate, how to distribute the types, and the advantages and disadvantages of its use must all be based on the national economic capacity, market economic trends, and commercial economic conditions for management. Remittance business is not just about issuing remittances. The layout of remittance lines, the consideration of the height of the exchange rate, and the pre-adjustment of the amount of remittance must also be those who are familiar with the market situation and familiar with the domestic and foreign economic and financial conditions to be able to consider surplus and deficit and plan ahead. The achievements of the post office in concurrently handling savings and remittances have also been developing in recent years. If banking experience and financial theory are combined to proceed, there is an immeasurable hope for development. Now it is said that since savings and remittance affairs have not yet developed, there is no need for banking specialization. This is like people in the Xianfeng and Tongzhi years saying that since the affairs of letter offices have not yet developed, there is no need to establish post offices. It is equally ridiculous. From the second point of view, the union obviously misunderstood. After the establishment of the Savings and Remittance Bureau, the business of savings and remittance, in addition to the head office having special responsibility for management, design and operation, is still handled by the post office. Therefore, the Savings and Remittance Bureau and the post office are actually one body. Why is it called separation? Savings and remittance affairs already have a head office to specialize in its responsibility. Why is it called non-specialized governance? Not only that, the profit of the Savings and Remittance Bureau is the profit of the post office, and the budget and final accounts of the Savings and Remittance Bureau are also the budget and final accounts of the entire postal service. The Savings and Remittance Bureau and the Post Office General Bureau are both directly under the jurisdiction of the Ministry. From the government's perspective, they are both part of handling postal affairs. To say that these affairs were previously managed concurrently by the Post Office General Bureau and could be developed, but now that the Savings and Remittance Bureau is in charge, it cannot be developed, is really incomprehensible. Moreover, the benefits of division of labor and cooperation are recognized by economists. Now it is said to be a situation where both sides will lose, which is unheard of. From the third point of view, the Savings and Remittance Bureau is only handling the affairs of postal savings and remittances. Its funds are still the assets of the entire postal service, which is no different from the time when savings and remittance affairs were subordinate to the Post Office General Bureau. This kind of statement by the union is similar to the result of the separation of the post office and the Savings and Remittance Bureau. The post office and the Savings and Remittance Bureau have not separated, as can be seen in the regulations of the bureau. Article 9 of the Postal Savings Regulations passed by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the National Government also states that the repayment of postal savings principal and interest is guaranteed by the postal service. The guarantee of postal savings has always been certain. After the establishment of the Savings and Remittance Bureau, there has been no change to this regulation, and there has never been any intention to change it. I don't know why the people in the union are shooting without a target. As for the expenditure of the head office, the annual budget is no more than 100,000 yuan, while the annual discount for postal remittances used to cost up to more than 300,000 yuan. After the establishment of the bureau, if it can reduce this expenditure to one-tenth, it will reach more than 300,000, which is more than enough to cover expenses. Why worry about wasting public funds? From the fourth point of view, domestic remittances, although limited in various circumstances, are unavoidable, but banks often restrict remittances and sometimes even refuse to remit. Now it is said that once a special bureau is established, there will be no restrictions on large amounts of remittances, causing difficulties for inland post offices. It is a misunderstanding of banking economics. Moreover, the personnel who handle remittances in the future will have general planning, coordination, and consideration methods, so there is no need to worry about it. From the fifth point of view, it is more about postal administration, and the union should not make wild guesses. As mentioned earlier, savings and remittance affairs should be managed by banking specialization and postal personnel to assist. Therefore, we have to solicit additional talent. In addition to most of the personnel being transferred from the post office and still receiving postal treatment, those newly hired are not postal personnel. How can we use postal regulations to discipline them? In short, I am in charge of transportation and have the responsibility to innovate the system and benefit the people for all the affairs under my jurisdiction. At the same time, I also value the history of our country's postal service and will never ignore it. The establishment of the Savings and Remittance Bureau is to make postal affairs develop doubly and strive to compete with Europe, America, and Japan. The personnel of the Postal Workers' Union have been serving in the post office for many years and should cherish the cause they are engaged in. Even if there are opinions due to unfamiliar circumstances, they should explain the truth to the Ministry. Now they have published it in the newspaper first, and now they have submitted a presentation to the Ministry, requesting to forward it to the National Government for reconsideration and cancel the previous order. Such interference in administration is really incomprehensible. The Ministry has now criticized it based on reason, and I cannot help but feel sorry for this.

The Postal Workers' Union's Letter to All Circles

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union's Letter to All Circles Regarding the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau says: To all compatriots from all walks of life: Our China Post has been in operation for more than 30 years. It has been difficult to create, and it has relied on the efforts of our postal workers to revolutionize and recover the entire postal rights from the hands of imperialism. Only then can we have today's achievements. In China, where all industries are declining, the post office should be the first to win glory for the nation and support the face of the country. However, domestic construction has not been developed for many years, and political changes have not been settled, which has affected the reduction of postal routes, and the number of bureaus in the interior has decreased rather than increased. The scope of the current bureaus has been reduced, and the treatment of workers has been delayed in improving. All these are great obstacles to the development of postal affairs, and tens of thousands of postal workers are racking their brains to find a way out to pray for the bright future and live up to the trust of their compatriots. Unexpectedly, in recent years, all the conspiracies to destroy the post office have been like a spring tide, and they will not stop until the entire post office is submerged and destroyed together. There was the previous traitorous and postal contract of Sino-American Aviation. In the end, our postal workers expressed their indignation, and all circles of society were deeply aware of the righteousness and rose up to awaken. The authorities dared to move and order the cancellation. Now, the ink of opposition has not dried, and the bad news of destruction has arrived again. What is this? It is the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, which will open on March 15. The Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau is named to develop savings and remittances, but in fact it is a butcher's knife for ambitious people to destroy the post office. Compared with the Sino-American contract, although the main body is different between China and foreign countries, the result of destroying the post office is even more cruel and sharp. As for planning the development of savings and remittances, what else can our postal workers say? It is exactly what we are bowing our heads and seeking. However, the way of development should be urgent first and then slow, and it is appropriate to consolidate the foundation first, and then flourish the branches and leaves. Our country's savings and remittance business has not yet developed, so we must first seek improvement and gradually seek development, so that the scope will be expanded day by day and the foundation will be consolidated. Then, for the convenience of management, divide the management and determine the number of bureaus to be established according to the size of the business scope. All countries in Europe, America, and Japan are the same. At the beginning, how should we first seek improvement from the business itself, which is the way to first consolidate the foundation? If we are ignorant of the construction procedures, but only to Europe, America, and Japan, which have been created by decades of hard work, Huang Huang is eager for success and is curious, and wants to reach it once in China, which is very poor, this person is either very stupid, or has another intention. It will be seen that the roots are not firm, and the branches, leaves, and tree itself are withered. The day when the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau is established is the day when the great post office will be destroyed. The lesson of the past of Sino-American Aviation can be learned. Can we not be horrified? According to today's newspaper, the Minister of Communications told people that the Savings and Remittance Bureau is only responsible for special savings and remittance design, and ordinary savings and remittance business is still handled by the post office, etc. If we want to separate the Savings and Remittance Bureau, why not transfer all the savings and remittance affairs to the head office? This kind of makeshift problem is self-evident, and false words are used to cover up. Now, I tell the authorities that if you do not want the post office to be destroyed, please stop the establishment, so as not to repeat the same mistakes as the Sino-American Aviation contract. If you must go your own way and act arbitrarily, then Chairman Chiang's strict order to reduce the over-needed organs has just been issued, and the party discipline is strict, and the national law is unavoidable. At this time, please do not make the dream of stealing the country again. The association is anxious and distressed, sad and screaming, for the post office and for the country, and does not care about it. I would like to sincerely announce it, and hope that all compatriots from all walks of life will pay attention to their interests and rise up to plan it together. Sincerely, Shanghai Postal Workers' Union, February 26.

The Municipal Health Bureau Strictly Prohibits Illegal Gratuities 131

The Municipal Health Bureau has discovered that shops have the illegal practice of giving gratuities to health inspectors. In addition to sending the health inspectors who received illegal gratuities to the Public Security Bureau for investigation according to Wang's law, it also issued a public notice yesterday, roughly saying: (1) The bureau's field staff and health inspectors are only responsible for abiding by the scope and undertaking investigation or guidance matters. The investigation or guidance situation must be reported back to the bureau. If the matter is more important, the bureau will send personnel to review it separately. If the public is not harmed, the bureau will never be demanding. The investigation or guidance personnel have no possibility of covering up or making things difficult. If you try to do so with illegal gratuities or bribes, it will not only be completely in vain, but also lose your personality because of such base behavior. (2) Even those who should be detained and punished out of necessity, the bureau must notify the competent district of the Public Security Bureau with an official document for execution, or take them to the bureau for interrogation. The bureau's field staff has no right to dispose of it freely. In addition, the fines received by the bureau or the various districts of the Public Security Bureau, no matter how much, must be filled out with an official receipt with the official bureau seal and given to the person being fined. If this official receipt is not filled out, it is illegal. You can report it to the Public Security Bureau and its districts or to this bureau to prevent Changming's extortion and facilitate the investigation of various agencies. (3) If anyone pretends to be a health official and demands money from the public, please be responsible for reporting it or handing it over to the guard police, and report it to the bureau immediately for investigation according to law. (4) This bureau has always taken corruption as a major taboo for its staff. If dereliction of duty is found, it will never be shielded. I hope the public will report it at any time based on the facts and be careful not to slander, so as not to violate Article 180 of the Criminal Law of false accusation. (5) Both giving and receiving bribes are illegal acts. Articles 128 and 129 of the Criminal Law have clearly stipulated the crimes. In the future, if anyone gives illegal gratuities or bribes to the personnel of this bureau, they will be reported to the court for punishment.

The Second Administrative Meeting of Baoshan County Opens 132

Preparatory Meeting Held Yesterday

The second administrative meeting of Baoshan County opened on the 26th (yesterday) in the auditorium of the county government. There were a total of 20 members. The seats were signed. The preparatory meeting was held at 9 am. Fourteen members attended. County Chief Wu Jianong presided over the meeting, and Chief Secretary Zhu Shiying recorded it. The rituals were as usual. A total of 38 important cases were proposed, and the report events included: 1. The first item of Article 2 of the Organizational Rules of this meeting, naturally members, was revised by the fourth county government meeting to be the county chief, the secretaries of the county government, the section chiefs of each section, the bureau chiefs of each bureau, the director of the farm, and the district chiefs of each district. 2. This meeting has three fewer natural members than the previous one and one fewer hired member. 3. Whether there are any amendments to the rules of procedure of this meeting. If amendments are required, please discuss them. 4. Appoint members of each group for review: (Finance Group) Yuan Xitao, Wang Zhongqi, Wang Cheng, Bei Jietai, Zhu Shiying, Lu Fengpu; (Public Security Group) Wang Zhonglin, Shen Jing, Wang Zhongqi, Yin Shuqi, Sun Qixian; (Construction Group) Huang Cengmu, Tao Qingfeng, Shi Langcun, Yan Guangen, Zhu Bao, Ji Zhonghe; (Education Group) Pu Wengui, Wang Qingyue, Wang Cheng, Wang Zhonglin; (Autonomy Group) Yang Weixiong, Wang Qingtao, Wang Zhonglin, Wang Zhongqi, Sun Qixian. Proposed items: 1. The proposal to amend the rules of procedure of this meeting. It was decided that Article 10 should be amended to: "The duration of this meeting is tentatively set at five days. When necessary, the chairman may change it at his discretion." 2. Discuss the method of electing the vice chairman. It was decided to use a secret ballot. Member Yin Shuqi was elected to count the votes. In the voting election, Wang Zhongqi won nine votes and was elected as the vice chairman. At 1 pm, the review members of each group reviewed the proposals. The official meeting will be held today (27th).

Instruction to Abolish the Baojia System 133

The Shanghai County Government previously received an order from the Jiangsu Civil Affairs Department, stating that the Baojia system in various counties in Jiangsu Province has more disadvantages than advantages. We should immediately verify whether it should be abolished. The former County Chief Lu, because the procedures for land measurement and valuation in this county have not yet been completed, and it is difficult to abolish it at present, presented it to the Civil Affairs Department for review. Now, Minister of Civil Affairs Miao found that the counties have different opinions on the preservation and abolition of the Baojia. He immediately submitted it to the Provincial Government Committee meeting for approval. It should be abolished uniformly. All the original duties of the Baojia should be managed by the township chief's office, etc. The Shanghai County Government has already received instructions from the Civil Affairs Department to the county, ordering immediate compliance with the abolition. Therefore, County Chief Leng has already instructed the County Finance Bureau and all districts to comply with it.

The Municipal Government Announces the Provisional Regulations for the Public Security Bureau to Handle Registration and Passport Visa Certification 134

(Continued from yesterday)

Chapter 2 Passports: (Article 9) All Chinese who travel abroad for travel or business and apply for Chinese passports to go abroad shall comply with the provisional measures for passports issued by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. (Article 10) People from non-treaty countries who apply for a registered passport and have not received a passport issued by their government shall come to the bureau in person to present their registration certificate of the bureau and fill in a registration form, and bring two 4.5-inch half-length photos of themselves. The photo fee is six yuan and the stamp fee is two yuan. (The above passport is valid for one year.) (Article 11) People from non-treaty countries who apply for inland passports shall come to the bureau in person to present their registration certificate of the bureau and fill in a registration form, and bring two 4.5-inch photos of themselves (add one more for traveling in more than one province, and so on). The photo fee is two yuan and the stamp fee is one yuan. (The above passport is valid for three months.) Article 12) The provisions of Articles 10 and 11 shall apply to the former Russians and Soviet Russians.

Chapter 3 Visa: (Article 13) Chinese and people from non-treaty countries who have passports to go abroad and come to the bureau for visa extension before the expiration date shall fill out a request form in person and bring two 4.5-inch photos of themselves. The visa fee is six yuan (the previous visa extension is valid for one year). (Article 14) People from treaty countries who hold passports signed by their government and come to the bureau to request a visa to travel or preach in the inland, or pass through various ports in China to exit the country, shall fill in a registration form in person and bring three 4.5-inch photos of themselves. The visa fee is three yuan. This visa extension is valid for three months. Those who ask to travel back and forth will pay an additional two yuan for the visa extension, which is valid for one year. (Article 15) People from treaty countries who have inland travel passports issued by their consulate in this city and sent to this bureau for endorsement shall bring three 4.5-inch photos of themselves. The endorsement fee is two yuan and the stamp fee is one yuan. (Article 16) People from non-treaty countries or people from countries without consular jurisdiction who hold round-trip travel passports issued by Chinese officials in other ports shall come to the bureau in person within ten days after arriving in Shanghai, fill out a request form, and bring one 4.5-inch photo of themselves to request verification. After verification, they may request a visa. The visa fee is two yuan and the verification is free. (Article 17) The provisions of Articles 13 to 16 shall apply to the former Russians and Soviet Russians. (To be continued)

Unification of the Value of Foreign Coins for Tram and Bus Fares in the North and South Municipalities 135

The trams and buses in the Chinese and Concession areas of this city have slightly suppressed the price of foreign coins according to the market price. The transportation companies in the North and South Municipalities have different prices for foreign coins, which are not uniform. A few days ago, the Municipal Executive Committee and the Jiangwan Branch of the Businessmen's Association sent letters to the Municipal Public Works Bureau one after another, asking them to transfer the order to the Chinese Public Bus Company to charge passengers with double coins or auxiliary coin coupons at market prices, and not to deliberately suppress them. The bureau then divided and ordered the companies concerned to discuss a unified method and submit it for approval. Subsequently, the China Merchant Electric Company, the China Merchant Public Bus Company, and the Hুনan Public Bus Company jointly replied with the reasons why coins and auxiliary coin coupons could not be used at market prices, which were roughly: (1) Most of the trams are short-distance, and less than 10% of passengers buy tickets of more than ten points. The highest fare for buses does not exceed two coins. The fares are trivial, and the time is short. If all passengers use copper coins to buy tickets, the ticket sellers are already overwhelmed. If coins are added, they need to find copper coins and identify the silver color, which is difficult to handle. Moreover, the stations are close to each other. To avoid missing tickets, it will inevitably delay the journey, which is detrimental to public transportation companies and business. Therefore, lowering the price of coins is a passive remedy, aimed at reducing the use of foreign coins, which is completely different from deliberately suppressing the price for trickery. (2) Recently, counterfeit lead coins are rampant. It is still the second thing that the ticket seller is negligent and deceived during the hasty receipt. It is especially worried that this will cause disputes, such as disputes over authenticity and errors in delivery. These are all worthy of consideration. Moreover, according to the average calculation of the fare, if one out of ten passengers buys a ticket with double coins, the fare paid by the other nine passengers is only enough for one person to find. If coins are used at market prices, passengers will use coins to buy tickets to avoid the trouble of carrying and exchanging copper coins. The burden is great. Moreover, the market price varies, and disputes are inevitable. (3) Trams have been running in the Chinese area for more than ten years, and buses have also been around for many years. Passengers have been accustomed to preparing the fare copper coins in advance when taking the bus. Moreover, there are many money shops in this port, and they are close to the stations, which are eye-catching and very convenient for exchange. Therefore, passengers have not felt the pain of suppressed prices or any difficulties in fact. It is also said that the price of coins on the concession tram is the same as in the Chinese area, and the length of the line and the number of passengers are twice that of the Chinese area. The reason why no one has risen up to question is that they all know the difficulties of the transportation business and the special circumstances and understand and sympathize with each other. Based on these reasons, the company and others publicly planned to fix one coin at 20 copper coins and one auxiliary coin coupon at 24 copper coins, so as to meet the purpose of collecting fewer coins. It is now learned that the bureau has verified that the reason is legitimate and the price is fair. It has approved it for record and has sent letters to the Municipal Executive Committee and the Jiangwan Branch of the Businessmen's Association to inform them.

American Residents Plan to Contest for Board of Directors of the Public Works Department 137

Proposed to Hold a Mock Election First

The Ta Wan Pao reports: Since Ms. Smith, the American Commercial Commissioner, was nominated as a candidate for the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department, it has stirred up a political competition among the expatriates in the Public Concession. When the news of Ms. Smith's candidacy was announced last Saturday, the American residents of this port were shocked by this unprecedented news of a woman running for election in Shanghai, as if by a sudden thunderclap. After recovering from the shock, in addition to the originally nominated Mr. Carney and Reverend Burden, they further nominated Mr. Tucker, the longest-serving broker in Shanghai, as the third male candidate to compete against her. How the election will ultimately turn out is difficult to predict at this point. However, it is heard that there is an organization among the American residents that intends to find a way to inform all concession voters of their two preferred candidates. If this is not done, it is feared that nine out of ten of the four American candidates will be defeated. Therefore, these people intend to hold an informal vote first, which is scheduled to take place at the meeting of the American Chamber of Commerce in the American Club on Friday. The two candidates who receive the most votes will be considered the people that the American residents prefer to be elected. Then, they will disclose this to the newspapers to indirectly inform the voters of all countries. Otherwise, the two candidates with fewer votes will automatically withdraw from the election. Apart from this, there is no other way to save them from defeat. Because there are already eight British candidates and two Japanese candidates. If the American residents nominate four more candidates, it is feared that none of the four will be able to be elected in the future.

City-Wide Defense Corps Training Conference 139

The Shanghai Special City Defense Corps is currently being actively reorganized by the Reorganization Committee. Yesterday afternoon, the North and South Shanghai Offices jointly convened the leaders, deputy leaders, and instructors of the corps in each district at the Qiaojia Road Office to hold a training conference. A total of sixty to seventy people attended. The General Instructor of South Shanghai, Fan Ju, and the General Instructor of North Shanghai, Hua Pu, presented the following points for discussion and resolution: (1) The training time is limited to one and a half hours per day. The timing, whether morning or evening, shall be determined by each district corps based on practical convenience. (2) For academic subjects, the instructors of each district shall, according to their jurisdiction, go to the North and South Shanghai Offices once a week for training by the General Instructor, who will then teach the corps members. The books to be used are as follows: Infantry Drill Regulations, Internal Affairs Regulations, Shooting Manual, Disciplinary Orders, Gun Maintenance Methods, Army Etiquette, Mental Training Speeches, all military knowledge, and Field Service. (3) Technical training shall be implemented in accordance with the prescribed books. (4) The training time is limited to three and a half months, starting from March 1. (5) Periodic inspections shall be conducted once a month. The date shall be determined by the General Instructor at any time and notified in advance. (6) To encourage the corps members, those who have the fewest absences and the best performance during the training period will be given prizes by the Reorganization Committee to encourage them.

Request to Include Anti-Drug Week in the New Calendar 140

Letter from the Anti-Drug Association to the Social Affairs Bureau

The Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau is currently preparing a new calendar for next year. The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association believes that the Anti-Drug Movement Week, held annually by the Association from October 1 to 7, is a movement to awaken the public to unanimously reject drugs. The date of Anti-Drug Week should be included in the calendar in order to promote it forever and widely. The Association had previously submitted a request to the Ministry of Interior, which was approved for implementation. The Ministry of Interior has consulted the Ministry of Education and forwarded it to the Astronomical Institute of the Academia Sinica for consideration. The Association specifically sent a letter to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, requesting that the date of Anti-Drug Week be included when preparing the calendar for next year, it is said.

Plea for Disaster Relief from Disaster Victims in Shan County, Western Henan 141

To All Newspapers: In the counties of Shan, Jianbao, and Luoyang in western Henan, we have suffered years of drought, coupled with banditry, resulting in countless people starving, displaced, and dying. Those who are fortunate enough to survive are also in extreme distress beyond words. Last winter, we were fortunate to have the Red Swastika Society establish porridge kitchens, which allowed us to barely survive. However, the disaster area is vast and there are many disaster victims. Even with the efforts of one association, it is ultimately difficult to reach everyone. Therefore, we humbly request all the great philanthropists in various ports to show great compassion and generously provide disaster relief, so that the remaining lives of the fortunate survivors will not end up in the realm of hungry ghosts. The merit and virtue of this act are immeasurable. We also earnestly request the newspapers to appeal on our behalf. We are overcome with gratitude and humbly beseech you.
